  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1a5b3eac-f394-4c77-86d3-5bfcb252dbd3'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13775795144117736561"><i> Mensagem </i> é o único livro de poemas de Fernando Pessoa publicado em português durante a sua vida. É também "realmente um só poema", como escreveu, dada a unidade perfeita conseguida pelo seu canto das grandezas passadas da nação - que se reflectem no futuro, potenciadas pelo Quinto Império.<br/><br/>Sem a simetria de composição nem a vastidão narrativa da epopeia clássica, é a obra</span>
  <span id="freeText13775795144117736561" style="display:none"><i> Mensagem </i> é o único livro de poemas de Fernando Pessoa publicado em português durante a sua vida. É também "realmente um só poema", como escreveu, dada a unidade perfeita conseguida pelo seu canto das grandezas passadas da nação - que se reflectem no futuro, potenciadas pelo Quinto Império.<br /><br />Sem a simetria de composição nem a vastidão narrativa da epopeia clássica, é a obra minimal de um Supra-Camões concentrado na construção de um mito, o de D. Sebastião, entendido como a síntese da ousadia dos heróis anteriores e como a promessa de um "dia claro" por vir.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13775795144117736561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3409193439" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3409193439" />
    <a title="Luís" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/117399210-lu-s"><img alt="Luís" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598708286p2/117399210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3409193439?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luís" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luís" href="/user/show/117399210-lu-s">Luís</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789726170082" href="/book/show/10245336-mensagem">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/117399210-lu-s?shelf=portuguese-literature">portuguese-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/117399210-lu-s?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/117399210-lu-s?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/117399210-lu-s?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3409193439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17167128259092546182"><b>"Message"</b> is a message of hope to the broken man. It is old Europe charged with a conquering history but which no longer dares to do anything. Her face turned to the sea - not the cramped ocean of the Romans, but the infinite sea of the soul - she looks to the future with nostalgia. Portugal dreams of a past where the will to seek new lands was more substantial than the fear of storms. Pessoa, messianic to the point, invokes the audacity of a king to come and the duty of man: the will to be.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38740406-mensagem">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21575078-florencia?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21575078-florencia?shelf=pessoanism">pessoanism</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1562461669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12091619858443916449">I'll have to rewrite this a bit. I'm slowly changing my opinion - they are my own and not other people's thoughts with different expressions, so all changes, great and small, may happen in a day...<br/><br/>*<br/><blockquote>And it is, after all, as good a way as any of solving the problem of existence to get near enough to the things and people that have appeared to us beautiful and mysterious from a distance to be able to satisfy ourselves that they have neither mystery nor beauty. <br/>— Proust</blockquote><br/>I want that quote on my skin, </span>
  <span id="freeText12091619858443916449" style="display:none">I'll have to rewrite this a bit. I'm slowly changing my opinion - they are my own and not other people's thoughts with different expressions, so all changes, great and small, may happen in a day...<br /><br />*<br /><blockquote>And it is, after all, as good a way as any of solving the problem of existence to get near enough to the things and people that have appeared to us beautiful and mysterious from a distance to be able to satisfy ourselves that they have neither mystery nor beauty. <br />— Proust</blockquote><br />I want that quote on my skin, though I'm not fond of whole paragraphs on one's body. Perhaps on the ceiling. Nevertheless, I want it near me; it's an antidote for the sense of wasted time. One has to try, that's always preferable to uncertainty. From a distance, book covers might look enticing, and authors one holds dear might caught one's attention. And when one finally gets in touch with the book, finally discovers its real essence, then one is in a better position to form an opinion. Sometimes we're lucky; other times, the more we get acquainted with the book, the more we realize it's not what it seems. As with people. <br />This poetry collection by wondrous Pessoa is an ode to his dear Portugal. He extols the virtues of its past with his delectable and mystifying verse. As usual, reading about patriotic hopes mixed with grandezas passadas da nação is not my forte. I'm sadly losing interest but hoping for a grand finale.<br /><br /><br />March 03, 18</span>

<div id="review_1811340361" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1811340361" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143117-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571421692p2/3143117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1811340361?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3143117-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789723717686" href="/book/show/31820188-a-mensagem-e-outros-poemas-sobre-portugal">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=portuguese-lit">portuguese-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=lusofonos">lusofonos</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1811340361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer871175471558461191">Great article about a show on Pessoa in Madrid<br/><br/>Pessoa del “fim do mundo”<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://cultura.elpais.com/cultura/2016/12/02/actualidad/1480702830_628977.html'>http://cultura.elpais.com/cultura/201...</a><br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed reading this collection of Fernando Pessoa poems that span his entire adult life. Pessoa writes in a lucid style, often poking fun at people, politics or institutions (and himself) but has a great love for his country (hence the subtitle "other poems on Portugal). For someone new to him and Portugal, the notes at the back fill one in sufficiently to understand the m</span>
  <span id="freeText871175471558461191" style="display:none">Great article about a show on Pessoa in Madrid<br /><br />Pessoa del “fim do mundo”<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://cultura.elpais.com/cultura/2016/12/02/actualidad/1480702830_628977.html">http://cultura.elpais.com/cultura/201...</a><br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed reading this collection of Fernando Pessoa poems that span his entire adult life. Pessoa writes in a lucid style, often poking fun at people, politics or institutions (and himself) but has a great love for his country (hence the subtitle "other poems on Portugal). For someone new to him and Portugal, the notes at the back fill one in sufficiently to understand the many names involved. And there are many. <br /><br />"Mensagem" is a masterful poem comparable to Elliot's "The Wasteland." The skill, the complexity and the verse resound with history, the age of discovery and the politics of his time. Divided into three parts, Pessoa reflects on the Portuguese coat of arms (the Kings), the sea (the heroes of discovery like Vasco de Gama, Ferdinand Magellan) and a more elusive, hidden or concealed present/future. Pessoa reflects on these characters as they developed Portugal and how they have been remembered. So unlike a poet sounding pompous about its history, Pessoa is more reflective, almost asking the reader to ponder the same. Beautifully written it becomes even more powerful knowing the history. The complete poem was only published just a year before Pessoa's death even though the poems had been written over a decade before. So it reads like a powerful final statement to his country. <br /><br />The other poems in this book range from early on from 1906 when he was an 18 year old and finish in 1935, the year of his death. Politics, history and social commentaries fill his head. There are so many to choose but a few stood out, like the untitled comparison of Spain and Portugal (Ó mãe Ibéria) or Fado da Censura or Marcha Fúnebre but for me the later poems had teeth. Many of these poems rally against Salazar, the long time autocratic prime minister such as "Poema de amor em estado novo" which is sadly funny. <br /><br />The weird irony is that as I read "Funeral March" as America chose a new president. Days later after reading the Salazar material and trying to understand what is happening in the world, Pessoa's words seem so much more alive. Is 1933 happening all over again? What is happening to the world? Perhaps there is some comfort in reading Pessoa now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="871175471558461191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/562488500" />
    <a title="Spike Gomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12727051-spike-gomes"><img alt="Spike Gomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347342213p2/12727051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/562488500?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Spike Gomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Spike Gomes" href="/user/show/12727051-spike-gomes">Spike Gomes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781905700271" href="/book/show/1712403.Message">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer562488500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16627241682999095209">I was not as struck by this book as I was by "The Book of Disquiet". I have a feeling it may be because much is being lost in the translation. Certainly, the Portuguese sounds much better than the English. I have some questions on word choice, but not knowing any better I defer to the translator.<br/><br/>In short, this book not written under a heteronym is a paean to the Portuguese nation and spirit. At times it certainly catches it. In others, I am completely left adrift (pun intended). This may be beca</span>
  <span id="freeText16627241682999095209" style="display:none">I was not as struck by this book as I was by "The Book of Disquiet". I have a feeling it may be because much is being lost in the translation. Certainly, the Portuguese sounds much better than the English. I have some questions on word choice, but not knowing any better I defer to the translator.<br /><br />In short, this book not written under a heteronym is a paean to the Portuguese nation and spirit. At times it certainly catches it. In others, I am completely left adrift (pun intended). This may be because I am not as knowledgeable in Portuguese history or poetics as I should be.<br /><br />I am not disappointed in it. I believe that my failure to be seized by the verses within is derived from my own failings, and I am certain I will revisit these pages again in the years to come. Certainly I greatly admire the spirit in which these poems were written. In this day and age when nationalism has become a dirty word, it's nice to see something written as an homage to a place and a people and its history that is not cynical, nor mawkish, nor chest-beating. It would be nice to see more along those lines. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16627241682999095209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3168031479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3010220204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12498969115620048717">This edition is the English translation of <i>Mensagem</i>. It gives the history of Portugal in a mini-epic, as seen in the symbols of that country's heraldic crest. The Translator's Preface describes the form as<blockquote>"more of a lyrical epyllion than an epic proper on the grand scale of Homer, Vergil, Dante, or Milton [...]"</blockquote>A significant theme in it takes place during the Age of Discovery. Portuguese explorers sailed the extent of the oceans to reach lands it had not known existed or had surmised existed. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText12498969115620048717" style="display:none">This edition is the English translation of <i>Mensagem</i>. It gives the history of Portugal in a mini-epic, as seen in the symbols of that country's heraldic crest. The Translator's Preface describes the form as<blockquote>"more of a lyrical epyllion than an epic proper on the grand scale of Homer, Vergil, Dante, or Milton [...]"</blockquote>A significant theme in it takes place during the Age of Discovery. Portuguese explorers sailed the extent of the oceans to reach lands it had not known existed or had surmised existed. The translation could be helpful if you want to read Pessoa's original in his language.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12498969115620048717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2385182163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2385182163?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HsiaoWen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HsiaoWen" href="/user/show/33519093-hsiaowen">HsiaoWen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781546481522" href="/book/show/39940746-message">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33519093-hsiaowen?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2385182163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8621964014260656739">This wonderful English translation of Pessoa's Mensagem is a fantastic insight into the once great seafaring nation. A series of poems on patriotic themes, Message is organised into three parts. The first section dedicates a poem to each fields of the Portuguese coat of arms, and various historical figures who played a role in the establishment of the nation. The second part refers to the age of Portuguese maritime exploration and its naval empire. The third part of Message is Pessoa's very inte</span>
  <span id="freeText8621964014260656739" style="display:none">This wonderful English translation of Pessoa's Mensagem is a fantastic insight into the once great seafaring nation. A series of poems on patriotic themes, Message is organised into three parts. The first section dedicates a poem to each fields of the Portuguese coat of arms, and various historical figures who played a role in the establishment of the nation. The second part refers to the age of Portuguese maritime exploration and its naval empire. The third part of Message is Pessoa's very interesting vision of the return of King Sebastiao, whom apparently some Portuguese still await for to this day. King Sebastiao is the Portuguese equivalent of King Arthur , and he is supposedly to bring about the Fifth Empire, a future utopic world of peace and understanding. <br /><br />The book also includes an informative introduction by the translator Mark Will, and a helpful set of end notes at the back, detailing the historical aspects of each poem.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8621964014260656739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It was clunky at times, probably mostly because of the translation, but also possibly because his style is more old fashioned than his contemporary English poets, whose work I’m more familiar with. <br/><br/>What I learned: “All beginnings are involuntary.”</span>

<div id="review_629623658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/629623658" />
    <a title="Jack Ferreira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12945730-jack-ferreira"><img alt="Jack Ferreira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357135145p2/12945730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/629623658?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Ferreira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Ferreira" href="/user/show/12945730-jack-ferreira">Jack Ferreira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789723704365" href="/book/show/13575713-mensagem">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer629623658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18081677985140890482">I have read better passages and poems from Fernando Pessoa than this book has to offer. This book may be small but it if you really want to understand the meaning and symbology it takes work (unless you are a huge portuguese history buff).<br/><br/>I personaly read it for some peace of mind. I didn't read it all when I was suposed to (in school) and had a hard time understanding what I did read. I really wanted to read and understand the whole thing since it's one of Portugals most beloved works.<br/>I'm not a</span>
  <span id="freeText18081677985140890482" style="display:none">I have read better passages and poems from Fernando Pessoa than this book has to offer. This book may be small but it if you really want to understand the meaning and symbology it takes work (unless you are a huge portuguese history buff).<br /><br />I personaly read it for some peace of mind. I didn't read it all when I was suposed to (in school) and had a hard time understanding what I did read. I really wanted to read and understand the whole thing since it's one of Portugals most beloved works.<br />I'm not an expert when it comes to poetry but in my opinion there are some really fantastic poems in here which I will definetly revisit.<br />Poems such as:<br /><i> O Dos Castellos (The Field of the Castles)<br />D. Dinis (King Dinis)<br />D. Fernando, Infante de Portugal (Fernando, Infante of Portugal)<br />Afonso de Albuquerque (Afonso de Albuquerque)<br />O Quinto Império (The Fith Empire)<br />Terceiro (Third)<br />Antemanhã (Before Dawn)</i><br />The problem for me is that there are also mediocre ones that in turn bring the whole book down. I'll even venture to say a couple came across as filler (e.g. <i>Calma/Calmness</i>), which to me makes sense since it's widely known he rushed the book toward the end in order to have it ready for submition to a poetry competition.<br /><br />The overarching themes and symbology are the best part and tie the book toguether very well. The patriotism doesn't feel obnoxious, in fact it feels very endearing and was nice to see the author spread his countries wings.<br /><br />I will say this book does not lend itself well to an english translation. If you can't read portuguese but want to read something by Fernando Pessoa definetly don't start with this one. His other works are a lot more adaptable and he even has some english written works.<br /><br />Pleasent read but not the best Pessoa has to offer. <br /><br /><b> 3.5/5 </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18081677985140890482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer361165489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1297325948486391431">Very good, very interesting, but far from being the masterpiece of Portuguese poetry, in my opinion and unlike the opinion of most people. It's not even comparable to "Os Lusíadas" by Luís de Camões, so far from its refinement, symbolism, passion, organization and beauty, which is, actually, the masterpiece of poetry, probably even in a world scale. We can't argue that "Mensagem" it's better just because it's easier to understand: please give me better arguments. I regard this interesting work b</span>
  <span id="freeText1297325948486391431" style="display:none">Very good, very interesting, but far from being the masterpiece of Portuguese poetry, in my opinion and unlike the opinion of most people. It's not even comparable to "Os Lusíadas" by Luís de Camões, so far from its refinement, symbolism, passion, organization and beauty, which is, actually, the masterpiece of poetry, probably even in a world scale. We can't argue that "Mensagem" it's better just because it's easier to understand: please give me better arguments. I regard this interesting work by Pessoa as a lower quality attempt to update "Os Lusíadas" or to present an epic in the same topic. Something wrong with this? No. But it's lower quality. Anyway, it give us some eternal quotes, namely about this feeling of "being Portuguese", and it's of the finest moments of the Portuguese poetry in the 20th century. In general, I just have to say that this is mandatory for the Portuguese poetry study but it's completely overrated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1297325948486391431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3536061903" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3536061903" />
    <a title="Ronan Gonçalves Figuerêdo " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/121023069-ronan-gon-alves-figuer-do"><img alt="Ronan Gonçalves Figuerêdo " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599392844p2/121023069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3536061903?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronan Gonçalves Figuerêdo " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronan Gonçalves Figuerêdo " href="/user/show/121023069-ronan-gon-alves-figuer-do">Ronan Gonçalves Figuerêdo </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3536061903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17669614175438510169">It is a considerably quick-reading book. It was Fernando Pessoa's only book edited in his lifetime. Pessoa is considered one of the greatest poets of the Portuguese language and, therefore, of universal literature. This book is composed of nationalist poetry. The poem “Mensagem” is relatively short, but it is of immense historical and literary grandeur. Despite needing a prior knowledge of the history of Portugal, Mensagem, it is a very rich work.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2622559077" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2622559077" />
    <a title="Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21042457-ryan"><img alt="Ryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534731361p2/21042457.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2622559077?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan" href="/user/show/21042457-ryan">Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781905700271" href="/book/show/1712403.Message">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Hardcore Pessoa Fans, Lovers of Portugal</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21042457-ryan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21042457-ryan?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21042457-ryan?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21042457-ryan?shelf=portugese">portugese</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2622559077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8010814600434070358">As someone who steeped myself in <i>The Book of Disquiet</i>, I found it difficult to appreciate this work as much. Although it is a great and poetical ode to Portugal, it feels like an emulation of some other great poet, though I know not who. By Pesssoan standards, I find this to be somewhat disappointing. If it were done by some other, less legendary writer, I'd think better of it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Maggie Hesseling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11154648-maggie-hesseling"><img alt="Maggie Hesseling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357497829p2/11154648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3446447773?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie Hesseling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie Hesseling" href="/user/show/11154648-maggie-hesseling">Maggie Hesseling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789895553662" href="/book/show/34230727-message">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11154648-maggie-hesseling?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3446447773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1448134724124282411">This was my first foray into the work of Pessoa. What a lovely collection of poetry about the history of Portugal. I was quite taken with some of the poems about the royalty and the explorers/navigators. Also, the artwork in this edition is wonderful.<br/><br/>I do recommend that you skip over the first 2 or 3 poems and then come back to them at the end. His poetic style requires a little getting used to, but after reading the entire book and coming back to the first few they really fell into place. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2249771985" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17026219180878003213">I believe in-order to truly enjoy poetry you must read the original text written in it’s original language. I also believe that 50% of the poetry meaning will be lost in the translation process. <br/><br/>My favorite from this book is: MENSAGEM/five/Sebastian I/ King of Portugal,<br/><br/> it goes like this:<br/><br/>“Mad, yes, mad, for I sought magnificence<br/>Which Luck chose to deny. <br/>In myself I lacked the confidence; <br/>Thus where the sands do lie<br/>That which I was remained, not that which am I.<br/><br/>Others took my madness from me<br/>With </span>
  <span id="freeText17026219180878003213" style="display:none">I believe in-order to truly enjoy poetry you must read the original text written in it’s original language. I also believe that 50% of the poetry meaning will be lost in the translation process. <br /><br />My favorite from this book is: MENSAGEM/five/Sebastian I/ King of Portugal,<br /><br /> it goes like this:<br /><br />“Mad, yes, mad, for I sought magnificence<br />Which Luck chose to deny. <br />In myself I lacked the confidence; <br />Thus where the sands do lie<br />That which I was remained, not that which am I.<br /><br />Others took my madness from me<br />With all it did comprise.<br />Without madness what shall a man be<br />But a virile beast of size<br />An empty corpse which multiplies?”<br /></span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YYJDCw/A3BgpBUzzCSzGRp7GVlzCFLkNAYurk6RCTRbwWJS561vUxzGO9Gav8Hk89Socs5e9UvxiStDYFP8xdQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9ILzc/dWbgHUfmgSBCRC/3bnWNg682S4XansaFRKvEFlWCTBE81m3sz10Iei+P2FHQsSN29aj0k+aJcj5PfAIg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

O livro foi publicado no Porto em 1888. A acção de Os Maias passa-se em Lisboa, na segunda metade do século XIX, e apresent<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12395148235672586210\" style=\"display:none\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #15\n\nOs Maias é uma das obras mais conhecidas do escritor português Eça de Queiroz. O livro foi publicado no Porto em 1888. A acção de Os Maias passa-se em Lisboa, na segunda metade do século XIX, e apresenta-nos a história de três gerações da família Maia. A acção inicia-se no Outono de 1875, quando Afonso da Maia, nobre e pobre proprietário, se instala no Ramalhete com o neto recém formado em Medicina. Neste momento faz-se uma longa descrição da casa - &quot;O Ramalhete,&quot; cujo nome tem origem num painel de azulejos com um ramo de girassóis, e não em algo fresco ou campestre, tal como o nome nos remete a pensar. Afonso da Maia era o personagem mais simpático do romance e aquele que o autor mais valorizou, pois não se lhe conhecem defeitos. É um homem de carácter, culto e requintado nos gostos. Em jovem aderiu aos ideais do Liberalismo e foi obrigado, por seu pai, a sair de casa e a instalar-se em Inglaterra. Após o pai falecer regressa a Lisboa para casar com Maria Eduarda Runa, mas pouco tempo depois escolhe o exílio por razões de ordem política. Há em Os Maias um retrato da Lisboa da epóca. Carlos, que mora na Rua das Janelas Verdes, caminha com frequência até ao Rossio (embora, por vezes, vá a cavalo ou de carruagem). Algumas das lojas citadas no livro ainda existem - a Casa Havaneza, no Chiado, por exemplo. É possível seguir os diferentes percursos de Carlos ou do Ega pelas suas da Baixa lisboeta, ainda que algumas tenham mudado de nome. No final do livro, quando Carlos volta a Lisboa muitos anos depois, somos levados a ver as novidades - a Avenida da Liberdade, que substituiu o Passeio Público, e que é descrita como uma coisa nova, e feia pela sua novidade, exactamente como nos anos 70 se falava das casas de emigrante. O romance veicula sobre o país uma perspectiva muito derrotista, muito pessimista. Tirando a natureza (o Tejo, Sintra, Santa Olávia...), é tudo uma choldra ignóbil. Predomina uma visão de estrangeirado, de quem só valoriza as civilizações superiores - da França e Inglaterra, principalmente. Os políticos são mesquinhos, ignorantes ou corruptos (Gouvarinho, Sousa Neto...); os homens das Letras sao boémios e dissolutos, retrógrados ou distantes da realidade concreta (Alencar, Ega...: lembre-se o que se passou no Sarau do Teatro da Trindade); os jornalistas boémios e venais (Palma...); os homens do desporto não conseguem organizar uma corrida de cavalos, pois não há hipódromo à altura, nem cavalos, nem cavaleiros, as pessoas não vestem como o evento exigia, as senhoras traziam vestidos de missa. Para cúmulo de tudo isto, os protagonistas acabam vencidos da vida. Apesar de ser isto referido no fim do livro, pode-se ver que ainda há alguma esperanca implícita, nas passagens em que Carlos da Maia e João da Ega dizem que o apetite humano é a causa de todos os seus problemas e que portanto nunca mais terão apetites, mas logo a seguir dizem que lhes está a apetecer um &quot;prato de paio com ervilhas,&quot; ou quando dizem que a pressa não leva a nada e que a vida deve ser levada com calma mas começam a correr para apanhar o americano (eléctrico). Mais do que crítica de costumes, o romance mostra-nos um país - sobretudo Lisboa - que se dissolve, incapaz de se regenerar. Quando o autor escreve mais tarde A Cidade e as Serras, expõe uma atitude muito mais construtiva: o protagonista regenera-se pela descoberta das raízes rurais ancestrais não atingidas pela degradação da civilização, num movimento inverso ao que predomina n\'Os Maias.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12395148235672586210\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n Movia-me à desconfiança o ser ele triste, sem interpolação de risos, sombrio, e rematado por catástrofe de confranger o ânimo dos leitores, que se interessam na boa sorte de uns, e no castigo de outros personagens. De nome <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5864442969748592218\" style=\"display:none\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #5\n\nJosé Maria de Eça de Queiroz (Póvoa de Varzim, 25 de novembro de 1845 — Neuilly-sur-Seine, 16 de agosto de 1900), escritor e ensaísta, foi um dos nomes mais importantes da literatura portuguesa. De nome completo José Maria de Eça de Queirós nasceu a Novembro de 1845, numa casa na Praça do Almada, em Póvoa de Varzim. O seu pai, José Maria de Almeida de Teixeira de Queirós, nascido no Brasil e vindo para Portugal com um ano de idade, provinha de uma família de magistrados perseguidos pelos seus ideais liberais que defendiam uma doutrina constitucional. Eça foi internado no Colégio da Lapa, no Porto, de onde saiu em 1861, com dezasseis anos, para a Universidade de Coimbra, onde estudou Direito. Num ambiente boémio da cidade universitária de Coimbra estes jovens reuniam-se para trocar ideias, livros e formas para renovar a vida política e cultural portuguesa, que estava a viver uma autêntica revolução social com a introdução dos novos meios de transportes ferroviários que traziam, todos os dias, novidades do centro da Europa, influenciando esta geração para novas ideologias e valores. Foi nesse grupo que Eça conheceu os futuros escritores e poetas, Teófilo Braga, Ramalho Ortigão, Guerra Junqueiro, Guilherme de Azevedo, Oliveira Martins, entre outros; mas sobretudo, foi aí que travou amizade com Antero de Quental, um jovem carismático a quem os membros do grupo chamavam de líder e que incentivou os restantes a seguir e a difundir as então recentes correntes ideológicas e literárias europeias: o Positivismo, o Socialismo e o Realismo-Naturalismo. Notabilizou-se pela originalidade e riqueza do seu estilo e linguagem, nomeadamente pelo realismo descritivo e pela crítica social constantes nos seus romances mas, tal como o crítico literário, Jacinto Prado Coelho disse: &quot;foi mais analista social do que psicólogo; ironizou Portugal porque muito o amava e o queria melhor.&quot;<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5864442969748592218\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7816.Fernando_Pessoa">About Fernando Pessoa</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7816.Fernando_Pessoa"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1427039317p3/7816.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7816.Fernando_Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,282
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14472613802031851727">Fernando António Nogueira Pessoa was a poet and writer.<br/><br/>It is sometimes said that the four greatest Portuguese poets of modern times are Fernando Pessoa. The statement is possible since Pessoa, whose name means ‘person’ in Portuguese, had three alter egos who wrote in styles completely different from his own. In fact Pessoa wrote under dozens of names, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/322304.Alberto_Caeiro' title='Alberto Caeiro' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alberto Caeiro</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/145525.Ricardo_Reis' title='Ricardo Reis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ricardo Reis</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1231596._lvaro_de_Campos' title='Álvaro de Campos' rel='nofollow noopener'>Álvaro de</a></span>
  <span id="freeText14472613802031851727" style="display:none">Fernando António Nogueira Pessoa was a poet and writer.<br /><br />It is sometimes said that the four greatest Portuguese poets of modern times are Fernando Pessoa. The statement is possible since Pessoa, whose name means ‘person’ in Portuguese, had three alter egos who wrote in styles completely different from his own. In fact Pessoa wrote under dozens of names, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/322304.Alberto_Caeiro" title="Alberto Caeiro" rel="nofollow noopener">Alberto Caeiro</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/145525.Ricardo_Reis" title="Ricardo Reis" rel="nofollow noopener">Ricardo Reis</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1231596._lvaro_de_Campos" title="Álvaro de Campos" rel="nofollow noopener">Álvaro de Campos</a> were – their creator claimed – full-fledged individuals who wrote things that he himself would never or could never write. He dubbed them ‘heteronyms’ rather than pseudonyms, since they were not false names but “other names”, belonging to distinct literary personalities. Not only were their styles different; they thought differently, they had different religious and political views, different aesthetic sensibilities, different social temperaments. And each produced a large body of poetry. Álvaro de Campos and Ricardo Reis also signed dozens of pages of prose.<br /><br />The critic Harold Bloom referred to him in the book The Western Canon as the most representative poet of the twentieth century, along with Pablo Neruda.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14472613802031851727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

"<br /><br />(...)Tudo vale a pena<br />Se a alma não é pequena.<br />Quem quere passar além do Bojador<br />Tem que passar além da dor. "<br /><br />Triste de quem é feliz!<br />Vive porque a vida dura.<br />Nada na alma lhe diz<br />Mais que a lição da raiz -<br />Ter por vida a sepultura."<br /><br />Ser descontente é ser homem. "<br /><br />Tenho meus olhos quentes de água. "<br /><br />'Screvo meu livro à beira-mágoa. "<br /><br />Quando, meu Sonho e meu Senhor?&rdquo;</span>
